<div id="review_146902749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146902749" />
    <a title="Kyami" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4752987-kyami"><img alt="Kyami" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429190375p2/4752987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146902749?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyami" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyami" href="/user/show/4752987-kyami">Kyami</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4752987-kyami?shelf=romance-paranormal">romance-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4752987-kyami?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4752987-kyami?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4752987-kyami?shelf=strong-female-heroine">strong-female-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4752987-kyami?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146902749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12778920576614298080"> The Last Vampire is my absolute favorite, no contest, young adult vampire romance book. I've read this book many many times throughout my teen years. 10 years later, i'm still in love with it. I decided to read it again after reading the twilight series. Twilight can't even compare to the last vampire stories!! This is the original YA vampire series, before Twilight, Vampire Diaries, Morganville, House of Night . get the picture? Besides Anne Rice, Christopher Pike turned me (pun inteneded) ont</span>
  <span id="freeText12778920576614298080" style="display:none"> The Last Vampire is my absolute favorite, no contest, young adult vampire romance book. I've read this book many many times throughout my teen years. 10 years later, i'm still in love with it. I decided to read it again after reading the twilight series. Twilight can't even compare to the last vampire stories!! This is the original YA vampire series, before Twilight, Vampire Diaries, Morganville, House of Night . get the picture? Besides Anne Rice, Christopher Pike turned me (pun inteneded) onto the vampire, supernatural genre. He's created a monster, lol! <br /><br />This series will rock you. Using an intelligent and powerful voice, the last vampire, Sita, tells her five-thousand year story of light and darkness, evil and profound spirituality...in this series you will witness Sita's beginning and her end, and afterwards you will walk away shaken and hungry for more. <br /><br />Her struggle to find personal and spiritual maturity will intrigue any deep-thinking teenager (or adult, for that matter). The Thirst series doesn't waste time. This vampire's storytelling is concise, always suspenseful, heartfelt and a little ironic. Pike re-imagines the vampire legend, giving us vampires who are more powerful, more sophisticated and more dangerous than those in other teen-vampire books. Sita has lived and loved well throughout her life, and because of these vast experiences she is proficient in everything human--from our arts to our weapons to our hearts and souls, Sita is an expert. And that is good, because she'll need these skills to resist those who know what she is. <br /><br /> Pike retains what I think makes these books so enjoyable: Sita's contemplative introspection. Sita is different from other vampire genre characters I have encountered, in a very good way. Her introspective monologues are written in such a way that one can actually believe she has lived as long as she has. There are frequent flashbacks to her history, with each one relating (somehow) to her present predicament; I find this blend of the past and present highly satisfying and very realistic. It's nice to read and understand why she does what she does, and not simply read that she does it. <br /><br /> As soon as I read the first page of the first book, I just fell in love with the character, Sita/Alisa. This is not just another vampire story, it's a tale of love and loss and selflessness. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12778920576614298080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_117861532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117861532" />
    <a title="Chandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4177075-chandra"><img alt="Chandra" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117861532?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chandra" href="/user/show/4177075-chandra">Chandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117861532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14776441167647151238">The Last Vampire – Black Blood – Red Dice<br/><br/>Meet Alisa Perne. The things you know or think you know about vampires are purely fiction. Alisa is a five thousand year old vampire. She does not kill her victims for blood but drinks only enough and makes them forget and leaves them with no memory of it and no marks. She can also go out into the sunlight without any adverse effects like going up in flames. The sun does weaken her powers and makes her tired. She does not sleep in a coffin but in a bed an</span>
  <span id="freeText14776441167647151238" style="display:none">The Last Vampire – Black Blood – Red Dice<br /><br />Meet Alisa Perne. The things you know or think you know about vampires are purely fiction. Alisa is a five thousand year old vampire. She does not kill her victims for blood but drinks only enough and makes them forget and leaves them with no memory of it and no marks. She can also go out into the sunlight without any adverse effects like going up in flames. The sun does weaken her powers and makes her tired. She does not sleep in a coffin but in a bed and only needs a few hours to regenerate. She is not indestructible but is very hard to kill. She made a vow to her God, Krishna, not to make any more vampires so she is doing her best to live up to that promise. Also her creator and once lover has come back to destroy her and fulfill his vow to Krishna, which was to kill those he made. Only Alisa is left.<br /><br />Things seem to be changing when a PI finds out some interesting facts and wants to blackmail her for a million dollars. Not that she doesn’t have it but nobody should know anything personal about her so he is killed. His son is the only one left that can help her with the password to his father’s computer. She only wanted to clean up the mess. So she becomes Lara Adams and enrolls in High School.<br /><br />Alisa is tired of killing and wants to be left alone but not really alone. She seems the type of person to want what she can’t have which is to be human and be loved. She does find love and friendship in unsuspecting places but also hardship. She has spent so long without emotions that when she learns what they are, she starts to change. Live a little in her world and enjoy.<br /><br />Do you believe in vampires? Reincarnation? You will stretch your imagination a little with this book. I enjoyed reading it but it wasn’t in my top 10. It was easy to read and really leaves you hanging at the end. Well written and good storyline. I will buy the second one of this series soon. I can’t stand to not know what happens.<br /><br />Alisa’s story continues in THIRST No. 2</span>
  <a data-text-id="14776441167647151238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_76584797" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76584797" />
    <a title="Hailey Ray" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2795593-hailey-ray"><img alt="Hailey Ray" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76584797?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hailey Ray" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hailey Ray" href="/user/show/2795593-hailey-ray">Hailey Ray</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76584797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11750118542546309456">My favorite character in <i>Thirst-The Last Vampire</i> was Alisa Pern. I liked her because she was always so adventurous and fearless. She wasn’t afraid of anything. My least favorite character was Yaksha. He was continuously trying to kill her and I didn’t think that she deserved to die. He attempted to kill the one that she loved, but in that attempt, failed.<br/>	I kept reading the book, because there was just something always drawing me in and always something to keep my attention. The book was somethi</span>
  <span id="freeText11750118542546309456" style="display:none">My favorite character in <i>Thirst-The Last Vampire</i> was Alisa Pern. I liked her because she was always so adventurous and fearless. She wasn’t afraid of anything. My least favorite character was Yaksha. He was continuously trying to kill her and I didn’t think that she deserved to die. He attempted to kill the one that she loved, but in that attempt, failed.<br />	I kept reading the book, because there was just something always drawing me in and always something to keep my attention. The book was something that had plenty of suspense and enough drama to last a lifetime. My favorite line from the book was something that Alisa thought during a really rough situation. “There is love where there is my grace. There is no time to be thankful for what I have been given in my lifetime. I feel as if I will choke on my grief. He looks at me with his trusting eyes, and I must find a way to save him.”<br />	The author wrote this book for enjoyable reading. He wrote it so that he could write about a story with a twist. If I were to recommend this book to anyone, it would be to girls in high school, simply for the language and content. I would have to say that the end section of the book kept me captivated. She was trying to find ways to keep them alive, and there was so much drama in it, it was hard to put the book down.<br />	I thought about quite a few different endings to the book, but the actual one was something I wasn’t expecting. It was such a shock the way it ended. If this book was made into a movie, I would make it to where Ashley Tisdale would play Alisa Pern, Paul Wesley would play Ray, and Johnny Depp would play Yaksha.<br />	While reading the book, I felt several different things. At some points I felt happy, but at others I felt somewhat worried, I also felt some suspense, a bit sad, and excited.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11750118542546309456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_151473095" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151473095" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/228427-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577907766p2/228427.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151473095?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/228427-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/228427-andrea?shelf=read-young-adult">read-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/228427-andrea?shelf=read-paranormal">read-paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151473095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14466440303574534933">I wouldn't have picked this up on my own, but this was a gift. All things considered, it was a good choice for me since I like young adult fiction AND vampires. I also went through a Christopher Pike phase in my oh so long ago middle school years. (Although my husband...the wonderful gift giver did not actually know that. That said, I was intrigued by this book when I started reading it.<br/><br/>I was quickly disappointed. This book was actually four books in one and each was more disjointed than the las</span>
  <span id="freeText14466440303574534933" style="display:none">I wouldn't have picked this up on my own, but this was a gift. All things considered, it was a good choice for me since I like young adult fiction AND vampires. I also went through a Christopher Pike phase in my oh so long ago middle school years. (Although my husband...the wonderful gift giver did not actually know that. That said, I was intrigued by this book when I started reading it.<br /><br />I was quickly disappointed. This book was actually four books in one and each was more disjointed than the last. The main character Alisa (or Sita to her friends) is a (a 5,000 year old vampire). She didn't have much depth (and neither did the stories) beyond - I am a vampire. I am perfect, I am strong, I can do anything, I am invincible, Nothing can stop me. Oh by the way I like to kill and I don't feel bad about killing...it is who I am. There is something to be said about the fact that main character was secure in who (and what) she was and did not spend time trying to "become human" or "fit in" as in so many vampire books.<br /><br />And of course we find out that she IS invincible. BUT she doesn't learn or change or grow as a character. She was simply so cold (and arguably maybe that is how vampires would actually be...especially after being alive for 5,000 years) that I did not care one fig about who she was, what happened to her in the past, or in the present. <br /><br />There were some parts that were captivating and interesting to me (such as the mythos of how vampires came to exist) However, the entire story/book was so segmented (the books went from ancient vampire feud to modern day governmental research facility) that it was not enjoyable. My brain just kept going...huh??? Of course there is another book. I'm not going to go out and buy, but if I see it on a discounted rack somewhere I may consider picking it up and reading it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14466440303574534933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

		<td>
      
			<a class="actionLink" href="/topic/show/1033293-the-last-vampire-thirst">The Last Vampire&gt;Thirst</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hhlxuL6vgLx3F89tkXDRWmt/1ZNVMPvNHA49E3uezwG8PxhqBfFJ1NA8ewxmhduFvSAyW5u9dapHcHuitt09mw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ht2iufKwYwGDW5e8nbaVuwJsMjDWhmmn6EPZiCt37ask+8trSe6qaSRwI91qQ59k1DPV+BgL58CzPZ855jQfMQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer2173680634649284155">Christopher Pike is the pseudonym of Kevin McFadden. He is a bestselling author of young adult and children's fiction who specializes in the thriller genre.<br/><br/><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i> <br/><br/>McFadden was born in New York but grew up in California where he stills lives in today. A college drop-out, he did factory work, painted houses and programm</span>
  <span id="freeText2173680634649284155" style="display:none">Christopher Pike is the pseudonym of Kevin McFadden. He is a bestselling author of young adult and children's fiction who specializes in the thriller genre.<br /><br /><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i> <br /><br />McFadden was born in New York but grew up in California where he stills lives in today. A college drop-out, he did factory work, painted houses and programmed computers before becoming a recognized author. Initially unsuccessful when he set out to write science fiction and adult mystery, it was not until his work caught the attention of an editor who suggested he write a teen thriller that he became a hit. The result was Slumber Party (1985), a book about a group of teenagers who run into bizarre and violent events during a ski weekend. After that he wrote Weekend and Chain Letter. All three books went on to become bestsellers.</span>
